    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25654096" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1275921-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214696280p2/1275921.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25654096?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/1275921-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25654096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6846776947072224640">This is THE best bedtime story, in my opinion. It was a nightly ritual for my first daughter, and it holds a very special place in our hearts. When it says that the dad bunny leans down and kisses the little one's head, Leah would always lean down and kiss the picture. The page became a little scummy from kiddie goo, and it's PRECIOUS! I will forever cherish my little girl's kisses in the book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1581415792" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10440703150400468818">This is one of only three board books that continuously survive the purge because I simply can't bear to move it out. I see tiny, invisible handprints all over it, as it was a favorite of both of my children. I received this as a baby shower gift and have easily read it hundreds of times. That it is still occasionally requested at bedtime makes my heart happy. Beautifully illustrated, this story is so sweet that I have never been able to read the ending without a lump in my throat and a hitch in</span>
  <span id="freeText10440703150400468818" style="display:none">This is one of only three board books that continuously survive the purge because I simply can't bear to move it out. I see tiny, invisible handprints all over it, as it was a favorite of both of my children. I received this as a baby shower gift and have easily read it hundreds of times. That it is still occasionally requested at bedtime makes my heart happy. Beautifully illustrated, this story is so sweet that I have never been able to read the ending without a lump in my throat and a hitch in my voice. How much do I love this book? To the moon. More importantly, how much do my children love this book? To the moon and back. 5 stars.<br /><br />Update 2018: This once again has survived the year end, post-holiday purge. I tossed my beloved camouflage print Vans, my 1992 Cure concert T-shirt and several little monuments to my past that no longer serve me, but I simply cannot release this 11 year old, tattered board book. So on my shelf in the living room it remains, where it continues to make my heart happy.</span>

And I wonder if that was to put off going to bed?! Of course it is. <br/><br/>This is a great little book.   <span id="freeText10560057046814263619" style="display:none">Someone wanted a story before bed, but someone isn't listening. I wonder if that someone could be Indy boy? And I wonder if that was to put off going to bed?! Of course it is. <br /><br />This is a great little book. One that is a physical story as we do the actions along with the little hare, and the big hare. Our arms stretched wide or high, to show the love. This is a good little book for my son as he does not sit still for a story, but as it's about what 'we' do at home ie., 'I love you to the moon and back' or 'I love you more, I love you 10, I love you 20' - yes this is what we say between bed and closed door as a way to say goodnight - anything that creates harmony around here is a good thing. Recommended book for 2's through to the moon and back of age groups. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fathers</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21464507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18330892579337538523">One of the only books I can read to my daughter where the adult in the book is a male. Most of the books have no men or relegate the father to support-staff roles. <br/><br/>Having said that, the book is really a testosterone-fueled look at the competitive indoctrination of little boys. <br/><br/>Paraphrase of text:<br/><br/>Kid: I love you as million.<br/><br/>Dad: I love you a billion.<br/><br/>Kid: Can't you let me win once?<br/><br/>Dad: Only when you surpass my strength, then I will live vicariously through you. <br/><br/><br/>Despite this shortcoming, the illustr</span>
  <span id="freeText18330892579337538523" style="display:none">One of the only books I can read to my daughter where the adult in the book is a male. Most of the books have no men or relegate the father to support-staff roles. <br /><br />Having said that, the book is really a testosterone-fueled look at the competitive indoctrination of little boys. <br /><br />Paraphrase of text:<br /><br />Kid: I love you as million.<br /><br />Dad: I love you a billion.<br /><br />Kid: Can't you let me win once?<br /><br />Dad: Only when you surpass my strength, then I will live vicariously through you. <br /><br /><br />Despite this shortcoming, the illustrations are great. My daughter loves it.</span>

  <span id="freeText1219741284119525978" style="display:none">Okay this is my favorite book in the whole wide world, so I was surprised to see the number of less than favorable reviews.<br /><br />To the guy that thinks (and I use that word liberally) that this book is a allegory for socialism, really? I mean really???? Really?????<br /><br />To everyone else that thinks this book is about a "game of one-upsmanship" or it has a "undercurrent of competition between the parent and the child", You guys could not be more wrong.<br /><br />Is upsmanship even really a word?<br /><br />This book is about the nature of the love that exists between parent and child, no matter how much your children love you, I assure you that it will never be as much as you love them. That's what this book is about.<br /><br />I read this book to my daughter just last night and I've read it to her at least a hundred times. Every time I do, when I flip that last page and read the final sentence, I nearly cry. That's why this is my favorite book in the whole wide world!</span>

<div id="review_3109733380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3109733380" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3109733380?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763674489" href="/book/show/20708838-guess-how-much-i-love-you">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those Looking for Lovely Reassurance Tales for Younger Children</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=picture-books">picture-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=reassurance-stories">reassurance-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3109733380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15219091928013687618">Little Nutbrown Hare and his father, Big Nutbrown Hare, have what at first glance seems like a love competition in this sweet reassurance tale from Northern Irish author Sam McBratney and English illustrator Anita Jeram. As the younger hare declares his love, only to be continually outdone by his elder - <i>"I love you as high as I can reach,"</i> the son says, but his father can reach higher - it gradually emerges that the two are enacting a bedtime ritual in which their mutual love is reaffirmed, all</span>
  <span id="freeText15219091928013687618" style="display:none">Little Nutbrown Hare and his father, Big Nutbrown Hare, have what at first glance seems like a love competition in this sweet reassurance tale from Northern Irish author Sam McBratney and English illustrator Anita Jeram. As the younger hare declares his love, only to be continually outdone by his elder - <i>"I love you as high as I can reach,"</i> the son says, but his father can reach higher - it gradually emerges that the two are enacting a bedtime ritual in which their mutual love is reaffirmed, all while the elder tacitly signals his protection, and the younger his admiration.<br /><br />A contemporary classic for young children, <u>Guess How Much I Love You</u> was originally published in 1994, and is a book I have read many times over the years, although I am only now (in 2016) getting around to recording my response to it. This edition is a 20th Anniversary one, and contains a brief note from both author and illustrator. I've always loved this gentle tale, with its humorous and indulgent papa hare, and its cute-as-a-button hare son. McBratney perfectly captures their back and forth, just as Anita Jeram captures their loving bond in her charming ink and watercolor illustrations. I particularly love the contrasts between Big and Little Nutbrown Hare, as they gesticulate. Recommended most highly to anyone looking for reassurance tales for younger children!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15219091928013687618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_462307070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462307070" />
    <a title="Mike Spinak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14854887-mike-spinak"><img alt="Mike Spinak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442650071p2/14854887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462307070?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Spinak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Spinak" href="/user/show/14854887-mike-spinak">Mike Spinak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462307070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3685794845960612355">This may be my least favorite children's book that I've read to the kids. Even worse than the highly commercialized children's books devoid of any value which are made for nothing but the tie-ins to TV shows and toy sales. Guess How Much I Love You turns loving each other into a competition - and one where the child can never win against the parent. I like the idea of parent and child loving each other a lot, but this is so, so wrong of a way to communicate that theme. I found it unpleasant and </span>
  <span id="freeText3685794845960612355" style="display:none">This may be my least favorite children's book that I've read to the kids. Even worse than the highly commercialized children's books devoid of any value which are made for nothing but the tie-ins to TV shows and toy sales. Guess How Much I Love You turns loving each other into a competition - and one where the child can never win against the parent. I like the idea of parent and child loving each other a lot, but this is so, so wrong of a way to communicate that theme. I found it unpleasant and saddening. It just made me uneasy to read it. And not just me. Ms. K only had to read it to her kids once, before she got rid of it. She felt the same way about it that I did. Yuck. <br /><br />On a positive note, the illustrations are good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3685794845960612355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Just let the kid love you big and give him right back atcha. How frustrated that little nutbrown hare must feel. I think this is a book for parents not for children. And it's fucking sappy. However, Anita Jeram's illustrations are absolutely lovely so props to her and I'm going to find more of her work.</span>

<div id="review_2211096460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2211096460" />
    <a title="Gerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry"><img alt="Gerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580749249p2/1525599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2211096460?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerry" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry">Gerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780744581898" href="/book/show/853175.Guess_How_Much_I_Love_You">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2211096460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16498309407158574266">How much is much? Little Nutbrown Hare (LNH) thinks he knows but when he relates to Big Nutbrown Hare (BNH) he falls short whatever he does!<br/><br/>LNH is holding on to BNH's long ears as he is being taken to bed and LNH asks BNH if he knows how much he loves him. When BNH says that he couldn't guess how much, LNH stretches his arms out and shows him that the distance between the extremities of each is how much he loves him. Just to show how much he loves LNH, BNH stretches his arms out and says that is</span>
  <span id="freeText16498309407158574266" style="display:none">How much is much? Little Nutbrown Hare (LNH) thinks he knows but when he relates to Big Nutbrown Hare (BNH) he falls short whatever he does!<br /><br />LNH is holding on to BNH's long ears as he is being taken to bed and LNH asks BNH if he knows how much he loves him. When BNH says that he couldn't guess how much, LNH stretches his arms out and shows him that the distance between the extremities of each is how much he loves him. Just to show how much he loves LNH, BNH stretches his arms out and says that is how much he loves LNB. <br /><br />A little bit taken aback, LNH then stretches upwards as high as he can reach and says that is how much he loves BNH, who responds by stretching upwards and tells LNH that is the extent of his love ... and LNH realises that his arms are long!<br /><br />LNH tries a handstand and tells BNH that he loves him all the way up to his toes but once again he is thwarted as BNH picks him up, swings him high and says, 'And I love you all the way up to your toes.' So LNH then hops high and tells BNH that he loves him as high as he can hop. The latter responds by hopping so high that his ears touch the highest branches of the trees and he tells LNH that is how much he loves him!<br /><br />So LNH decides that he will try another strategy and he says, 'I love you all the way down the lane to the river' to which BNH responds with 'I love you across the river and over the hills.' LNH thinks that is very far and feels sleepy with all the thought he has put in. But just as he is beginning to feel too sleepy to think anymore he looks up at the sky and realises that nothing could be further than the sky. So he tells BNH, 'I love you right up to the moon' and BNH is obliged to say, 'Oh, that's far. That is very, very far.' LNH thinks that he has had the last word ...<br /><br />But as BNH puts him into his bed of leaves and kisses him goodnight, he lies down next to his youngster and he smiles and whispers to him, 'I love you right up to the moon - AND BACK.'<br /><br />Little Brown Hare just cannot win but he does know that the love between the two of them is immense.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16498309407158574266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201747984" />
    <a title="Airiz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4848495-airiz"><img alt="Airiz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420337239p2/4848495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201747984?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Airiz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Airiz" href="/user/show/4848495-airiz">Airiz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4848495-airiz?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4848495-airiz?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4848495-airiz?shelf=books-from-childhood">books-from-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4848495-airiz?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4848495-airiz?shelf=children-s-lit">children-s-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201747984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6722833031260892909">A shot of insulin, please! Sam McBratney's <i>Guess How Much I Love You</i> has lots of saccharine in it—but not to a point it’s cloying, just something that a dreamland-bound kid would surely enjoy. See, there’s no plot of any kind, just a pair of adorable, furry hares (I think they’re father and son) engaging in an equally cute contest on who loves the other more. Anita Jeram’s illustrations are perfectly endearing. I heard there’s a collection of this, and kid or not—geez I just turned twenty!—I’ll </span>
  <span id="freeText6722833031260892909" style="display:none">A shot of insulin, please! Sam McBratney's <i>Guess How Much I Love You</i> has lots of saccharine in it—but not to a point it’s cloying, just something that a dreamland-bound kid would surely enjoy. See, there’s no plot of any kind, just a pair of adorable, furry hares (I think they’re father and son) engaging in an equally cute contest on who loves the other more. Anita Jeram’s illustrations are perfectly endearing. I heard there’s a collection of this, and kid or not—geez I just turned twenty!—I’ll be glad to have them all. Who knows? I might read them to my own kids in the future. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6722833031260892909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91547480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91547480" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91547480?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=valentines-day">valentines-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=childrens-picture-books">childrens-picture-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91547480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4072065757678325614">This is a sweet story where the big bunny (maybe a daddy bunny?--nice touch as there are relatively few books with dads) and the little bunny try to express how much they love one another. The ending phrase seemed a bit trite but perhaps it's because I have heard the phrase so much now, on everything from t-shirts to wall art, that it seems cliche. Not sure if this book was the first one to use it...? </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_3254260736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3254260736" />
    <a title="Chantal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31954777-chantal"><img alt="Chantal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586070858p2/31954777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3254260736?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal" href="/user/show/31954777-chantal">Chantal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3254260736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17264191277872531099">A cute little book about how much one rabbit loves his child. The drawings were great and the story was simple but I had to laugh at times because it reminded me of ex boyfriend I had. Great book for kids about the meaning of love.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16949984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16949984" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/615496-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579701488p2/615496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16949984?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/615496-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16949984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14277857844074404086">OK--I don't get this book. I just picked it up at a thrift store, feeling like Jackson is probably missing out on a major rite of passage if he doesn't read this as a toddler, but I don't get it. So the big nutbrown hare has to outdo the little nutbrown hare every time? It's a competition, is it? Sure, it's pretty and all, but someone needs to explain to me why this is a classic. Is my Mom card going to be revoked for saying that?</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9iiqJapHYPMm/sa8xziEhM5VSaWOEqGtk9d0V4rbGrR8dnu7ocdQnqv4RaJtGO7s/w9cTL1cifHdn1bvE20iBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zPxl8BUXWCZ0lPH6+xMw54wvgo1CH1hOLVOOORVkbdtGorRuHpdoS/mScuRRM1qPvXWXZHFRcBJjG6yBjNJVag==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25838.Sam_McBratney">About Sam McBratney</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25838.Sam_McBratney"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1403555987p3/25838.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25838.Sam_McBratney">Sam McBratney
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
173
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16713078668703058778">The 1943 born Northern Ireland native started writing children's books when he was a teacher in his thirties, with the aim of helping out students who had trouble reading. But he continued writing for a more-personal reason: "the act of imagining simply makes me feel good," he says. The fifty-seventh book of Sam McBratney's career, and his first book with Candlewick Press, was the much-loved GUESS</span>
  <span id="freeText16713078668703058778" style="display:none">The 1943 born Northern Ireland native started writing children's books when he was a teacher in his thirties, with the aim of helping out students who had trouble reading. But he continued writing for a more-personal reason: "the act of imagining simply makes me feel good," he says. The fifty-seventh book of Sam McBratney's career, and his first book with Candlewick Press, was the much-loved GUESS HOW MUCH I LOVE YOU, which has sold an astonishing 15 million copies worldwide, and is available in 37 languages. "This is not the sort of thing you expect when most of your books have been remaindered," the author admits. "But, as the frog trapped in the milk discovered, if you keep going, sometimes you find yourself walking on cream cheese." <br /><br />Where does Sam McBratney get his inspiration? "I told my children stories when they were young," he says, "so when I write I try to think of what they would have liked." But there may be another source guiding his writing as well. The author's father--who worked as a type compositor with the BELFAST TELEGRAPH, and whose favorite books were westerns--is the person Sam McBratney credits for giving him his love of the English language. "Most of my picture books--GUESS HOW MUCH I LOVE YOU, THE DARK AT THE TOP OF THE STAIRS, JUST ONE!, and JUST YOU AND ME--explore the relationship between a big one and a wee one," the author notes. "The big one is not called the father in the stories, but that's what he is. Although my dad died before I became a writer, the father in my stories has a voice and a presence that he would have recognized and understood." <br /><br />In addition to authoring many books for children, Sam McBratney wrote radio plays for adults and a prize-winning collection of short stories. He received a degree in history and political science from Trinity College, Dublin, and worked for many years as a teacher. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16713078668703058778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
